# Charter
In compliance with the newly approved City Ordinance No. 1, Series of 2025, which officially supersedes City Ordinance No. 7, Series of 2018, Gordon College affirms its full adherence to the updated directives as mandated by the local government. The institution remains committed to aligning its policies and operations with the latest regulatory framework to ensure a lawful, effective, and community-responsive higher educational institution.

# College Seal
This is the official college seal/logo of Gordon College. This is to be used in legal and formal documents and correspondence of the College. The colors green and yellow signify the community college’s commitment to sustainable development or a development for all generations as it works towards environmental sustainability in its attainment of its vision, mission and goals. “Ulo ng Apo” represents the city of Olongapo where the local Higher Education Institution is based. This symbolizes the ability of its students to lead and make a difference in the community.
The torch illuminates a book which represents the ability to serve as a guiding light for others. It also shows how education is a beacon of light that nurture learning. It is strategically placed beneath the Ulo ng Apo signifying that knowledge must be used, not for knowledge’s sake, but more for the community which includes its stakeholders.
The circular wreath made of interlocking branches and leaves represents the unity and strength of stakeholders and its students who stand among the distinguished scholars the local HEI molded and developed. With the wreath of laurel leaves being a symbol of honor and victory, students, faculty and the leaders of the institution are expected to achieve victory over ignorance while remaining honorable and preserving integrity towards excellence.
The platinum colored shield placed behind the Ulo ng Apo represents the boldness of its students in pursuit of new horizons of unparalleled intellectual success. To remind its students staff and all the members of the institution to be bold and brave enough to explore and seek new opportunities beyond the four corners of the college towards the development of the community they belong to.
Under the shield is the year that Gordon College was founded. This represents the number of years of upholding its values. Three values guide the college, namely: excellence; character and service which shall guide the institutions’ trifocal function of instruction, research and extension.
The logo is in a form of circle, symbolizing the perfect fulfillment of a holistic educational process.

### Keywords: history, gc history, when founded, founded, established, background

# History of Gordon College
Gordon College was an off-shoot of the Olongapo City Training Center, then a training center for skilled manpower for employment at the former Naval facility of the United States. With the facility’s closure, and the slowing down of demand for skilled workers, City residents shifted to professional courses. The unavailability of affordable tertiary institutions for urban poor sector of the population led the City Government of Olongapo, during the incumbency of Hon. Katherine H. Gordon, then City Mayor, to open the Olongapo City Colleges through City Ordinance no. 9 series of 1999.
Initially, the College offered Bachelor of Science in Accountancy and Bachelor of Science in Computer Studies to 177 enrollees. Additional four-year programs were offered in the succeeding years to accommodate the demand of City residents for other programs.
City Ordinance no. 42 series of 2002 was passed in May 2002, providing a change in the name of Olongapo City Colleges to Gordon College, its present name, in honor of the Gordon family who greatly contributed to the development of the City of Olongapo. In the same year, the College was officially accepted as a member of the Association of Local Colleges and Universities (ALCU).
In 2004, a revision on the legal basis for the creation and operation of Gordon College was made through City Ordinance no. 36 series of 2004. In the same year, the College was granted by the Commission on Higher Education (CHED) Region III the certificate to operate with autonomy as per provisions of the Local Government Code of 19991. In addition to its undergraduate programs, the College opened its graduate programs in Education, Public Management and Business Administration.
In 2018, City Ordinance No. 07 series of 2018 was passed revising the charter of Gordon College subject to all Legal and Existing Rules and Regulations. This was superseded by City Ordinance No. 01 series of 2025 which was passed in 2025 that equipped Gordon College to expand its horizon for excellence to national and international level.

# Mandate and Function
Gordon College, formerly Olongapo City Colleges, is a local higher education institution established in 1999 under the City Government of Olongapo.
The College operates by virtue of City Ordinance No. 36, Series of 2004 and its amendment City Ordinance No. 1, Series of 2025 also known as the “ 2025 Revised Charter of Gordon College” that supersedes the City Ordinance No. 7, Series of 2018 . The proposed revision of the Charter of Gordon College aims to strengthen the promotion of excellence and delivery of education in the national and international level.
The Local Government of Olongapo supports and maintains its commitment to provide accessible and equitable distribution of opportunities to its constituents to acquire higher education, as well as, a responsive and relevant higher education institution.
### Legal Bases
* **CHED Memorandum Order No. 32, Series of 2006** – Policies, Standards and Guidelines on the Establishment and Operation of Local Colleges and Universities (LCUs);
* **CHED Memorandum Order No. 4, Series of 2007** – Implementing Rules of CM032, Series of 2006;
* **CHED Memorandum Order No. 42, Series of 2016** – Amendment of Article V, Section 5 and 12 of CMO 32, Series of 2006;
* **DILG Memorandum Circular No. 2009-67** – Guidelines on the Establishment of Local Colleges and Universities by Local Governments, and on the Operation of Higher Education Programs;
* **Republic Act No. 7722** – Higher Education Act of 1994;
* **Republic Act No. 9160** – Local Government code of 1991;
* **City Ordinance No. 1, Series of 2025** – 2025 Revised Charter of Gordon College
* **City Ordinance No. 7, Series of 2018** – Revised Charter of Gordon College of 2018;
* **City Ordinance No. 8, Series of 2010** – An Ordinance Amending the Legal Basis on the Creation and Operation of Gordon College;
* **Resolution No. 42, Series of 2002**– A Resolution Chaning the Name of Olongapo City Colleges to “Gordon College”;
* **City Ordinance No. 9, Series of 1999** – An Ordinance Creating Olongapo City Colleges

# Vision, Mission, Objectives, and Core Values
## Vision
A globally recognized local institution committed to innovative academic excellence, holistic and sustainable development, inclusivity, and community engagement.
## Mission
Produce empowered global citizens who create sustainable impact, uphold values of character, excellence, and service, and contribute to academic and societal development
## Strategic Objectives
1. **H**arness partnerships and linkages to produce graduates with global competencies aligned with the needs of the community and industry.
2. **O**rganize extension programs to sustain the greater impact of the institution to the community and environment.
3. **L**everage research outputs to improve existing knowledge and practices.
4. **I**ntegrate ethical principles and standards in the curriculum to strengthen the moral responsibilities of lifelong learners.
5. **S**upport continuous professional development and well-being of employees.
6. **T**ailor-fit student support services to ensure students thrive in the rapidly changing world.
7. **I**nvest in state-of-the-art facilities and technologies to enhance teaching, learning and research.
8. **C**ultivate a culture that embraces diversity and inclusivity.
## Core Values
* **Character.** Character is the foundation of a meaningful life. The institution strives to instill in students a strong moral compass, integrity, and a sense of responsibility for their actions. This includes fostering critical thinking skills, respect for diversity, and a commitment to a lifelong learning.
* **Excellence.** The institution provides a rigorous academic environment that challenges students to reach their full potential. Intellectual curiosity, innovation, and a pursuit of knowledge for its won sake is encouraged. It is believed that excellence is not just about achieving high grades, but also about developing the ability to analyze complex problems, think creatively, and communicate effectively.
* **Service.** Education empowers individuals to make a positive impact on their communities and the world. Students are encouraged to engage in service-learning opportunities that allow them to apply their knowledge and skills to real-world problems. The institution fosters a culture of social responsibility where students develop a sense of compassion and a desire to contribute to the betterment of society.

# Colleges
**Institute of Graduate Studies**
The mission of the Institute of Graduate Studies of Gordon College is to provide quality master’s degree programs and opportunities for continuing professional and career development for students whose academic preparation and personal characteristics foresee success in graduate studies. Each graduate program is firmly grounded in theoretical and empirical bodies of knowledge. Students are challenged to think critically and creatively, and to apply theories to practice in an atmosphere of inquiry and dynamic exchange with faculty and each other
**College of Allied Health Studies**
By 2025, the College of Allied Health Studies is envisioned to be a Center of Excellence in Allied Health Education in Region III and dedicated to being a forerunner in providing research-inclined instruction, evidence-based practice and community–responsive health care education committed to the holistic development of the human person.
**College of Business and Accountancy**
A center of excellence in accounting and business education that develops competitive leaders and professionals for providing professional training, innovative research and relevant extension services.
**College of Computer Studies**
The College of Computer Studies shall be the Center of Excellence in Information Technology and Computer Science for providing professional and technological training, scientific and innovative, and relevant community service
**College of Education, Arts and Sciences**
We envision the Gordon College-College of Education, Arts and Sciences to be a center of excellence in the field for providing professional training, innovative research and community service.
**College of Hospitality and Tourism Management**
To be a center of excellence in tourism and hospitality management with high standard through instruction, research and extension.

# Academic Affairs
Academic affairs is the institutional office that oversees a variety of academic programs and departments at a school. The head of this office supports curriculum initiatives, faculty hiring and promotion events, faculty research and teaching, and all academic departments and programs.
## Offices Under the Academic Affair’s Office
* Institute of Graduate Studies
* College of Allied Health Studies
* College of Business and Accountancy
* College of Computer Studies
* College of Education, Arts, and Sciences
* College of Hospitality and Tourism Management
* National Service Training Program
* Open and Distance Learning/ Vocational and Technical Education
* Cosme Y. Sering Library (College Library)
* Office of Instruction
* Educational Resources Development Unit

# Institutional Planning, Development, and External Affairs (IPDEA)
## Vision
An innovation hub for strategic development and global relations that fosters cross-cultural understanding and builds local and international linkages for academic excellence.
## Mission
Lead strategic planning and global engagement in Gordon College by facilitating inclusive collaboration and international partnerships to achieve academic excellence and empower global citizens.
## Offices Under IPDEA
• Quality Assurance and Accreditation  
• International Affairs Unit  
• Partnerships and Linkages Unit  
• Diversity, Equity and Inclusion Unit

# Office of the College President
This office exercises overall responsibility and supervision over the College. The Chief Executive Officer of the College which is the College President is responsible for the articulation of the vision, mission, goals and objectives of the College and the development and implementation of educational programs and policies to achieve them. The office is directly accountable to the Board of Trustees for the organization, administration and supervision of the College.

### Keywords: continuing students, returnees, cross enrollment, cross-enroll

# Continuing Students, Returnees and Cross Enrollment
## Continuing Students and Returnees
Continuing students are those who were previously enrolled in the College but unable to enroll for at least one semester and decided to continue studying in GC. These students have not requested for any transfer credential. They may have or have not filed for Leave of Absence.
Returning students are those who requested for transfer credentials but decided to re-enroll in the College. Returning students shall no longer be required to take the admission test.
## Cross Enrollment
* **GC Students to Enroll in Other Schools**
  + Students shall not be allowed to cross-enroll without proper consultation and consent from their respective College Deans. Students shall not be allowed to cross-enroll if the subject/course is not open during his/her last two semesters in the College. He/She shall request recommendation from his/her Dean and authorization coming from the College Registrar before he/she can cross-enroll to other colleges/universities.
* **Students from Other Schools to Cross-enroll in GC**
  + Students from other schools who would cross-enroll in GC should present a written permission from his school that he/she is allowed to enroll in GC.

# Freshmen Students
## Admission Requirements
Admission to Gordon College shall be open to Filipino citizens, both residents and non-residents of Olongapo City, Non-Filipino citizens, high school graduates, or passers of the high school equivalency certificate (PEPT), and shows evidence of being able to benefit from instruction. A NON-RESIDENT is defined as any individual who has lived less than one year in Olongapo City, is not registered to vote in Olongapo City and/or does not pay property taxes or contributes to the economic development of Olongapo City.
## New College Freshmen Students for Undergraduate Programs
* Admission to the chosen degree program will be based on an applicant’s Gordon College Admission Test (GCAT) results and previous high school/college academic records.
* Original copy of High School Report Card (F138/SF9) or Original ALS Certificate of Rating Secondary Level for ALS Passers
* Certificate of Good Moral Character
* Copy of Birth Certificate
* Medical Certificate (Issued by the Gordon College Clinic)
* Barangay Certificate of Residency
* One 2×2 picture

### Keywords: igs, graduate studies, master, graduate admission

# IGS (Institute of Graduate Studies) Students
To qualify for admission to the Institute of Graduate Studies, an applicant must meet the following general and specific standards:
1. Student must have a minimum undergraduate GPA of 2.00 or 85% (except NSTP and PE). Student with lower general average than the prescribed rating may be admitted to the master’s program on probation. While on probationary status, s/he is allowed to carry the maximum load of only six (6) units per term. S/he will be placed in full standing status after having obtained an average rating of 1.5 or better in the first 12 units.
2. Specific programs may have different requirement as well as additional requirements such as materials and a personal interview, to wit:
   1. Master in Public Administration
      * At least two (2) years of government/ public service in any capacity
   2. Master in Business Management
      * BS Commerce or BS Business Administration graduate
      * Non-business course graduate must finish 18 tool courses. While earning these units, s/he may enroll any two basic/major subjects in the MBM program.
      * At least two (2) years of relevant experience/ service.
   3. Master of Arts in Education
      * Should be an education graduate
      * For non-education graduate, at least 24 units of professional education in the undergraduate level.
      * At least two (2) years of teaching experience/ service.
   4. Master of Arts in Nursing
      * Should be a Registered Nurse
      * At least two (2) years of experience in nursing and/or related field.
3. Pass the qualifying examination and interview.
4. All applicants for admission must submit the following;
   * Original Transcript of Records from recognized colleges or universities (with remarks, “Copy for Gordon College” or “Granted Honorable Dismissal”).
   * Two ID pictures (2×2/passport size)
   * Certificate of Employment
   * A Php200.00 non-refundable fee for application processing.
   * Additional materials, if required by specific program.

### Keywords: student publication, the forefront, campus paper, student newspaper

# Student Publication
**The Forefront** is the official student publication of Gordon College located in Olongapo City Sports Complex, Donor Street, East Tapinac, Olongapo City 2200. Its office is located at Rm. 516, 5th Floor, GC Main Building.
The Forefront was reestablished on June 2009, after a four-year hiatus, with the desire to promote the development and growth of responsible journalism as a means of strengthening ethical values, encouraging critical and creative thinking, and developing moral character and personal discipline in accordance with the Campus Journalism Act of 1991 (R.A. 7079).
**THE LOGO**
The official logo of the Forefront, as appeared above, is consist of two elements and two colors.
A *quill or pluma* refers to the writing profession. Its color, red, symbolizes courage and sacrifice. A *stem of laurel leaves* signifies triumph. Its color, golden yellow, symbolizes the nobility of the writing profession. The quill and the stem of laurel leaves form a capital letter “F” which stands for The Forefront.
**General Principles and Objectives**
The Forefront lives with its tagline, **“Informing and Empowering.”** To be able to uphold with its battlecry for campus press freedom, the Editorial Board sets the following General Principles:
1. The Forefront shall serve primarily as a newspaper of and for the students. It shall protect and promote the constitutionally mandated rights of students to free speech and of expression. In addition, it shall protect and promote the students’ rights and welfare.
2. The Forefront, being a publication of the students devoted to the ideals of truth, shall pursue the mission of social transformation through active and responsible journalism.
3. The Forefront, being an independent institution, shall not be subjected to any form of censorship. In turn, the editors and staff shall see to it that the Forefront exercises academic and campus press freedom in accordance with the laws of the Republic of the Philippines. It shall also seek to protect and promote  
   press freedom by taking firm and assertive stance against elements endangering such right.
4. The editors shall respect the rights of other parties that are equally protected by the laws of the Republic of the Philippines, affording them the right and opportunity to refute or reply to criticism or comment hurled at them.
Along with this principles, The Forefront shall at all times strive to:
1. Inform the public (i.e. the general population of the College, including the administration and the general public outside the College) with news of relevance and interest;
2. Serve as a venue for campus opinion and in maintaining an atmosphere of free and responsible discussion and of intellectual exploration;
3. Provide an outlet for students’ suggestions for the betterment of the campus;
4. Develop students’ powers of observation and discrimination concerning relative merits of news articles and;
5. Provide an opportunity for journalistic and creative writing.
[](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/wp-content/uploads/2023/10/366944890_1400491360869874_3388834360043358186_n.mp4)

### Source: https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/gc-presents-one-thousand-students-in-graduation-rites

# GC presents one thousand students in graduation rites
[Image: GC presents one thousand students in graduation rites]
[Campus](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/campus/) [News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Thursday, July 10, 2025**
Gordon College’s (GC) 23rd Commencement Exercises saw a total of 1,016 passionate graduates walk in the aisle of Subic Bay Exhibition and Convention Center (SBECC) this year, donning their respective togas and sablays.
Amidst heavy rains, Cluster I filled the morning ceremony with 487 graduates from the College of Business and Accountancy (CBA) and Hospitality and Tourism Management (CHTM).
Meanwhile, 529 students from Cluster II’s College of Allied Health Sciences (CAHS), College of Computer Studies (CCS), and College of Education, Arts, and Sciences (CEAS) graced the stage during the afternoon rites.
The graduates are products of Free Higher Education (FHE) from the institution and taxpayers, who enjoyed it during their tenure.

# Gordon College proudly welcomes the CHEDRO III Technical Panel for Nursing
[Image: Gordon College proudly welcomes the CHEDRO III Technical Panel for Nursing]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Wednesday, June 4, 2025**
Gordon College proudly welcomes the CHEDRO III Technical Panel for Nursing, the Technical Evaluator for Nursing, and the Regional Quality Assessment Team (RQAT) for the evaluation of our Master of Arts in Nursing (MAN) Program on May 29–30, 2025.
This collaborative engagement forms part of Gordon College’s initiative to apply for the Certificate of Program Compliance (COPC) and reflects our commitment to quality assurance, academic excellence, and continuous improvement in graduate nursing education.

### Source: https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/responsibilities-of-the-data-subjects

# Responsibilities of the Data Subjects
Associated to the exercise of rights are responsibilities to respect the privacy of others and comply with Gordon College’s regulations in its administration of data privacy.
Data subjects shall have the following responsibilities:
1. Respect the data privacy rights of others;
2. Report any suspected security incident or personal data breach to Gordon College Data Protection Officer by sending an email or accomplishing OCP-DPU Form No. 4;
3. Provide Gordon College with true and accurate personal data and other information. Before submitting personal data of different people to Gordon College, obtain the consent of such people.
4. Not disclose to any unauthorized party any non-public confidential, sensitive or personal information obtained or learned in confidence from Gordon College; and
5. Abide by the policies, guidelines and rules of Gordon College on data privacy, information security, records management, research and ethical conduct. From time to time, check for and comply with updates on these policies, guidelines and rules. Students may also refer to their Student Handbook.

# Gordon College’s Newest Royalty Emerges
[Image: Gordon College’s Newest Royalty Emerges]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Tuesday, February 24, 2026**
JUST IN | The spotlight bedazzles the center stage as Gordon College’s newest royalty emerges on stage. Mr. Marc Anthony Acula from College of Business and Accountancy (CBA) and Ms. Charmyn KC Sierra from College of Hospitality and Tourism Management (CHTM) claim the crown as Mr. and Ms. Gordon College 2026.
These newly crowned icons are now set to carry the GCian pride to the regional and national stage, representing the institution in the Association of Local Colleges and Universities (ALCU) and the Local Colleges and Universities Athletic Association (LCUAA). | via Kana Maye Dueñas, The FOREFRONT

# PESO-TCLASS Visits Gordon College for BSN Program Benchmarking and COPC Preparation
[Image: PESO-TCLASS Visits Gordon College for BSN Program Benchmarking and COPC Preparation]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Friday, August 29, 2025**
Gordon College warmly welcomed the Public Employment Service Office – Tarlac Center for Learning and Skills Success (PESO-TCLASS) under the Provincial Government of Tarlac last August 26, 2025, for a benchmarking visit.
As part of their preparations to offer the Bachelor of Science in Nursing (BSN) program and apply for a Certificate of Program Compliance (COPC), the PESO-TCLASS delegation, headed by Dr. Maria Lira Reyes – PESO Manager and School Administrator, engaged with Gordon College to learn from our best practices in curriculum development, faculty qualifications, library and physical facilities, equipment, support services, and quality assurance systems. The visit provided them with valuable insights and guidance on meeting the minimum standards required for program compliance.
This knowledge-sharing initiative reflects Gordon College’s continued commitment to collaboration and capacity-building among academic institutions.
[#SDG4QualityEducation](https://www.facebook.com/hashtag/sdg4qualityeducation?__eep__=6&__cft__[0]=AZXKAVLrnMGfGqvROk8dTmDB6wq5FDLLRzLeas8DwK-SMD06Of8Lt3ungUOTPIsOVfSJXWXnp3TwsHEp8LkBi7uWLIQXjr88oLu0WZcEbXxCNW9i1eWTT7ALg_XBtCXjYVpCfZplPBB7V2NBxT74G4VMHSUgKaxb0yOSTpGATevh3K3T7bwkR4tzoWQjDT4utLpnP0Bi5ERWhyGof7HKSSh4jsRWWpOcI9UKN_sxgV7ttA&__tn__=*NK-y-R)

# THE FOREFRONT WINS BIG AT 5TH AOCPA
[Image: THE FOREFRONT WINS BIG AT 5TH AOCPA]
[ForeFront](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/forefront/) [OSWS](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/osws/) [News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Thursday, February 13, 2025**
SAN FERNANDO, Pampanga – The Forefront, the official student publication of Gordon College, garnered five awards at the 5th Assumption Outstanding Campus Press Awards (AOCPA) held at the University of the Assumption on January 27, 2025.
Thirty publications across Luzon participated in the competition, submitting a total of 278 entries according to Regina, the official student publication of the University of the Assumption.
The Forefront’s award-winning staff members are:
Patrisha Marie Pineda – 4th Most Outstanding Investigative Journalist
John Carlo Bermudez – 8th Most Outstanding Literary Writer
Stephanie Estrella – 8th Most Outstanding Opinion Writer
Lance Isaac Leon – 9th Most Outstanding Editorial Cartoonist
John Patrick Mateo – 10th Most Outstanding Feature Writer
The conference is an annual iteration of UA’s Regina in search for the most outstanding campus journalists in different categories across Luzon.

# RESCHEDULING OF ID PROCESSING (December 8, 2025)
[Image: RESCHEDULING OF ID PROCESSING (December 8, 2025)]
**Sunday, December 7, 2025**
[Image: 📢]
**NOTICE: RESCHEDULING OF ID PROCESSING**
Please be informed that the scheduled ID Processing on December 8, 2025 (Monday) has been rescheduled due to the non-working holiday.   
ID Processing will now be conducted on any day from December 9 to December 12, 2025 (Tuesday–Friday). Students may proceed on their preferred date within this period.   
We apologize for any inconvenience this may cause and appreciate your understanding.

# 3 studes earn top spots in CFMS and CMMS exams; GC produces new CPACE-certified undergrads
[Image: 3 studes earn top spots in CFMS and CMMS exams; GC produces new CPACE-certified undergrads]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Tuesday, December 23, 2025**
Francis Jerome De Jesus and Belynda Apog, 4th-year Bachelor of Science in Business Administration Major in Financial Management students, ranked 4th and 5th, respectively, in their assessment examinations. Meanwhile, Marketing Management major Michaella Soliven secured the 10th spot of her own.
In a post, the Center for Professional Advancement and Continuing Education, Inc. (CPACE Philippines) announced the passers of the Batch 25 Certified Financial Management Specialist (CFMS)® and Certified Marketing Management Specialist (CMMS)® assessment examinations on Thursday, December 18, and Friday, December 19, respectively.
De Jesus, 90.42%, and Apog, 90%, both broke into the Top 10 for the CFMS® assessment exam. On the flip side, Soliven cleared the CMMS® assessment with a rating of 86.67%.
Furthermore, 78 additional Financial Management from the College of Business and Accountancy (CBA) students cleared the assessment, bringing the institutional passing rate to 76.70%, while the results also saw one more taker pass the CMMS® exam.
CPACE Philippines totaled an overall passing rate of 69.88% and 80% for CFMS® and CMMS® examinations, respectively.
The assessment examinations were conducted via online and in-person formats, including Gordon College (GC) – Annex Bldg., from November 28 through December 13. | via Keane Rafael Abdon/The FOREFRONT

# GCian Alumni Makes Name on OSLP 2023
[Image: GCian Alumni Makes Name on OSLP 2023]
[Alumni](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/alumni/) [News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Wednesday, October 11, 2023**
Mr. Marko L. Aratea and Mr. Nieki E. Garigo, both alumni from Gordon College’s College of Education, Arts, and Sciences (CEAS), stand out as finalists during the award ceremony for Outstanding Student Leaders of the Philippines (OSLP) 2023 held at Teacher’s Camp, Baguio City, on October 1, 2023.
In an interview with The Forefront, Aratea and Garigo claimed that the Office of Student Welfare and Service (OSWS) and GC-CEAS had announced that they would represent the institution in the aforementioned competition and directed all requirements to Transforming Advocates and Champions (TRAC).
“I was astonished and exhilarated when it was announced that I was one of the top 20 finalists. Knowing that out of 135 applicants across our nation and at various colleges and universities, I was chosen. For me, I consider that one of the great achievements that I had,” Aratea said, reflecting on how he felt when he knew that he was one of the finalists.
While Garigo stated, “Syempre napasigaw ako that time, because bago pa dumating sa point na yan ay marami kaming dinaanang proseso at screening. I still remember the day where they conducted our final interview and sakto pang nakaduty ako sa Cooperating School ko for my practice teaching, and as in, medyo mahina ang signal niyan kaya during my 1-hour interview, ay naroroon ako sa ilalim ng manga ng Regional Science High School para maging stable ang internet, and sobrang naging successful naman ng interview dahil every time na may mga ganyang screening, kasi ako I always put in my mind na parang “kachikahan” ko lang ang interviewer at sobrang ganda ng discussion namin, especially yung point na may SDG pa sa question, like I am not ready that time dahil ang nasa isip ko talaga niyan ang lesson sa susunod na subject na tuturuan ko. But thank God because everything went well.”
They expressed their deepest gratitude to TRAC for the opportunity they attained and to their co-finalists from different schools. The representatives would also like to thank Gordon College, the GC Alumni Association, Inc., GC-RDCES, GC-OSWS, GC-CEAS, their families, and lastly, the Almighty God.
“Be who you are, be true to yourself, and always know your advocacy by heart and mind. Think of this competition as a way for you to raise your voice as a student leader, an advocate, and a champion,” Aratea said, while Garigo stated, “Be a leader na hindi tuta; be a leader na boses ng mag-aaral; be a leader who is pro-people, pro-student, and pro-community,” as their advice for those aspiring student leaders of the institution.
Aratea was also hailed as the champion for the Student Research Paper Presentation at the said event.

# 𝐌𝐗. 𝐆𝐂 𝐒𝐏𝐄𝐂𝐈𝐀𝐋 𝐀𝐖𝐀𝐑𝐃𝐒 𝐇𝐈𝐆𝐋𝐈𝐆𝐇𝐓𝐒
[Image: 𝐌𝐗. 𝐆𝐂 𝐒𝐏𝐄𝐂𝐈𝐀𝐋 𝐀𝐖𝐀𝐑𝐃𝐒 𝐇𝐈𝐆𝐋𝐈𝐆𝐇𝐓𝐒]
[OSWS](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/osws/) [News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Tuesday, February 20, 2024**
GORDON COLLEGE — As the competition arises, five- contestants received a triumphant win to special awards.
On a two-sets of awarding, Mx. Albert Panotes, Mx. College of Health and Allied Studies (CAHS) received the Mx. Congeniality, Mx. Beautiful Body, Best in Pride Attire, and Best in Formal Wear.
Meanwhile, Vench Paje, Mx. College of Education, Arts, and Sciences (CEAS), garnered the Best Advocacy Video and Best Casual Wear.
Furthermore, Josh Allen Bermudez, the Mx. College of Business and Accountancy (CBA) hailed as the Mx. Photogenic, Social Media Award, Mx. People’s Choice, and Best Talent.
And to end the night, Joshua Salgado, Mx. College of Hospitality and Tourism Management (CHTM) is awarded with Mx. Healthy Smile and Mx. Perfect Skin.
The contestants received a sash and certificate fully-proving that the title is theirs anymore.

# 𝐓𝐮𝐥𝐨𝐧𝐠 𝐃𝐮𝐧𝐨𝐧𝐠 𝐏𝐫𝐨𝐠𝐫𝐚𝐦 (𝐓𝐃𝐏) 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐓𝐞𝐫𝐭𝐢𝐚𝐫𝐲 𝐄𝐝𝐮𝐜𝐚𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧 𝐒𝐮𝐛𝐬𝐢𝐝𝐲 (𝐓𝐄𝐒) 𝐃𝐢𝐬𝐭𝐫𝐢𝐛𝐮𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧
[Image: 𝐓𝐮𝐥𝐨𝐧𝐠 𝐃𝐮𝐧𝐨𝐧𝐠 𝐏𝐫𝐨𝐠𝐫𝐚𝐦 (𝐓𝐃𝐏) 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐓𝐞𝐫𝐭𝐢𝐚𝐫𝐲 𝐄𝐝𝐮𝐜𝐚𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧 𝐒𝐮𝐛𝐬𝐢𝐝𝐲 (𝐓𝐄𝐒) 𝐃𝐢𝐬𝐭𝐫𝐢𝐛𝐮𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧]
**Thursday, December 11, 2025**
𝐀𝐍𝐍𝐎𝐔𝐍𝐂𝐄𝐌𝐄𝐍𝐓
𝐓𝐮𝐥𝐨𝐧𝐠 𝐃𝐮𝐧𝐨𝐧𝐠 𝐏𝐫𝐨𝐠𝐫𝐚𝐦 (𝐓𝐃𝐏) 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐓𝐞𝐫𝐭𝐢𝐚𝐫𝐲 𝐄𝐝𝐮𝐜𝐚𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧 𝐒𝐮𝐛𝐬𝐢𝐝𝐲 (𝐓𝐄𝐒) 𝐃𝐢𝐬𝐭𝐫𝐢𝐛𝐮𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧
To all 𝐥𝐢𝐬𝐭𝐞𝐝 𝐓𝐃𝐏 𝐚𝐧𝐝 𝐓𝐄𝐒 𝐠𝐫𝐚𝐧𝐭𝐞𝐞𝐬, please be advised that the claiming of your financial grants will be held at 𝐆𝐨𝐫𝐝𝐨𝐧 𝐂𝐨𝐥𝐥𝐞𝐠𝐞, 𝐅𝐮𝐧𝐜𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧 𝐇𝐚𝐥𝐥 (𝟑𝐫𝐝 𝐅𝐥𝐨𝐨𝐫) 𝐨𝐧 𝐃𝐞𝐜𝐞𝐦𝐛𝐞𝐫 𝟏𝟏–𝟏𝟐, 𝟐𝟎𝟐𝟓, 𝐟𝐫𝐨𝐦 𝟕:𝟎𝟎 𝐀𝐌 𝐭𝐨 𝟓:𝟎𝟎 𝐏𝐌.
This payout covers the following:
• 𝐓𝐃𝐏 𝐁𝐚𝐭𝐜𝐡 𝟕.𝟏 – 𝟐𝐧𝐝 𝐒𝐞𝐦𝐞𝐬𝐭𝐞𝐫, 𝐀𝐜𝐚𝐝𝐞𝐦𝐢𝐜 𝐘𝐞𝐚𝐫 𝟐𝟎𝟐𝟑–𝟐𝟎𝟐𝟒
• 𝐓𝐃𝐏 𝐁𝐚𝐭𝐜𝐡 𝟑 – 𝟏𝐬𝐭 𝐒𝐞𝐦𝐞𝐬𝐭𝐞𝐫, 𝐀𝐜𝐚𝐝𝐞𝐦𝐢𝐜 𝐘𝐞𝐚𝐫 𝟐𝟎𝟐𝟒–𝟐𝟎𝟐𝟓
• 𝐓𝐄𝐒 𝐋𝐢𝐬𝐭𝐚𝐡𝐚𝐧𝐚𝐧 𝟏𝟓 – 𝟏𝐬𝐭 𝐒𝐞𝐦𝐞𝐬𝐭𝐞𝐫, 𝐀𝐜𝐚𝐝𝐞𝐦𝐢𝐜 𝐘𝐞𝐚𝐫 𝟐𝟎𝟐𝟒–𝟐𝟎𝟐𝟓
[Image: 📄]
𝐑𝐞𝐪𝐮𝐢𝐫𝐞𝐝 𝐃𝐨𝐜𝐮𝐦𝐞𝐧𝐭𝐬
Please prepare the following complete documents :
1. 𝐓𝐡𝐫𝐞𝐞 (𝟑) 𝐩𝐡𝐨𝐭𝐨𝐜𝐨𝐩𝐢𝐞𝐬 of your 𝐬𝐭𝐮𝐝𝐞𝐧𝐭 𝐈𝐃 𝐨𝐫 𝐯𝐚𝐥𝐢𝐝 𝐠𝐨𝐯𝐞𝐫𝐧𝐦𝐞𝐧𝐭 𝐈𝐃 (𝐰𝐢𝐭𝐡 𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐧𝐚𝐭𝐮𝐫𝐞), each with 𝐭𝐡𝐫𝐞𝐞 (𝟑) 𝐬𝐩𝐞𝐜𝐢𝐦𝐞𝐧 𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐧𝐚𝐭𝐮𝐫𝐞𝐬
2. 𝐅𝐨𝐫 𝐀𝐮𝐭𝐡𝐨𝐫𝐢𝐳𝐞𝐝 𝐑𝐞𝐩𝐫𝐞𝐬𝐞𝐧𝐭𝐚𝐭𝐢𝐯𝐞𝐬 (𝐈𝐦𝐦𝐞𝐝𝐢𝐚𝐭𝐞 𝐅𝐚𝐦𝐢𝐥𝐲 𝐎𝐍𝐋𝐘) — all in 𝐭𝐡𝐫𝐞𝐞 (𝟑) 𝐜𝐨𝐩𝐢𝐞𝐬:
a. Original 𝐀𝐮𝐭𝐡𝐨𝐫𝐢𝐳𝐚𝐭𝐢𝐨𝐧 𝐋𝐞𝐭𝐭𝐞𝐫 with the grantee’s wet signature.
b. Photocopy of the 𝐬𝐭𝐮𝐝𝐞𝐧𝐭 𝐈𝐃 𝐨𝐫 𝐯𝐚𝐥𝐢𝐝 𝐠𝐨𝐯𝐞𝐫𝐧𝐦𝐞𝐧𝐭 𝐈𝐃 (with signature) of the grantee, each with 𝐭𝐡𝐫𝐞𝐞 (𝟑) 𝐬𝐩𝐞𝐜𝐢𝐦𝐞𝐧 𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐧𝐚𝐭𝐮𝐫𝐞𝐬.
c. Photocopy of the 𝐯𝐚𝐥𝐢𝐝 𝐠𝐨𝐯𝐞𝐫𝐧𝐦𝐞𝐧𝐭 𝐈𝐃 (with signature) of the authorized representative, each with 𝐭𝐡𝐫𝐞𝐞 (𝟑) 𝐬𝐩𝐞𝐜𝐢𝐦𝐞𝐧 𝐬𝐢𝐠𝐧𝐚𝐭𝐮𝐫𝐞𝐬.

• For those who have not yet submitted: Please provide your 𝐂𝐞𝐫𝐭𝐢𝐟𝐢𝐜𝐚𝐭𝐞 𝐨𝐟 𝐈𝐧𝐝𝐢𝐠𝐞𝐧𝐜𝐲 (Purpose: Educational Assistance).

# GC RECOGINZED AS INTERNATIONALIZATION CHAMPION (ICONS) FOR ITS PERFORMANCE IN THE TIMES HIGHER EDUCATION IMPACT RANKINGS 2025
[Image: GC RECOGINZED AS INTERNATIONALIZATION CHAMPION (ICONS) FOR ITS PERFORMANCE IN THE TIMES HIGHER EDUCATION IMPACT RANKINGS 2025]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Wednesday, December 10, 2025**
Today, the College was honored by the Commission on Higher Education for our outstanding achievements in global rankings, sustainability, ASEAN awareness, and internationalization during the Internationalization Champions of Nation-Building and Sustainability (ICONS) Awards 2025, held on December 10, 2025 (Wednesday), from 1:00 PM to 9:00 PM at the Philippine International Convention Center (PICC) in Pasay City.
The College was recognized for its high-impact sustainability initiatives, commendable performance in international rankings and ratings, pioneering efforts to advance internationalization, and valuable contributions to United Nation’s Sustainable Development Goals (SDGs).
This recognition is the result of our Internationalization initiative, based on the released ranking results for this year in the Times Higher Education Impact Rankings 2025.
The College extends its gratitude to Hon. Rolen C. Paulino Jr., City Mayor; Hon. Cristabelle Marie C. Paulino, Committee on Education Chairperson; Dr. Imelda DP. Soriano, College President; Dr. Kristin Joy A. Mendoza, Vice President for Institutional Planning and External Affairs; Ms. Precious S. De Castro, Coordinator of the International Affairs Unit; other Vice Presidents, BOT Members, College Officials, Management Council Members, faculty members, administrative personnel, and all other stakeholders who contributed to this achievement.

# Gordon College GAD Focal Point System Conducts Benchmarking Visit at PLM
[Image: Gordon College GAD Focal Point System Conducts Benchmarking Visit at PLM]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Monday, August 11, 2025**
Representatives from various departments of Gordon College, serving as members of the Gender and Development (GAD) Focal Point System, successfully concluded a benchmarking visit to Pamantasan ng Lungsod ng Maynila (PLM) last August 08, 2025. The activity aimed to strengthen the College’s GAD programs by learning from PLM’s best practices in promoting gender equality, inclusivity, and institutional development.
The delegation was warmly welcomed by PLM officials and staff. The visit featured comprehensive presentations on PLM’s Diversity, Equity, and Inclusion (DEI) framework, gender-responsive policies, and student-centered initiatives. Delegates also toured PLM’s academic and administrative facilities, including specialized units dedicated to personnel and student support and welfare.
An open forum provided an opportunity for Gordon College representatives from different units to engage with PLM counterparts, exchanging strategies on implementing GAD-related projects, integrating gender perspectives in policies.
This activity reinforces Gordon College’s commitment to fostering a gender-responsive, inclusive, and equitable academic environment through continuous learning and partnership with other higher education institutions.

### Source: https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/gordon-college-celebrates-26th-founding-anniversary-with-successful-fundation-run-2025

# Gordon College Celebrates 26th Founding Anniversary with Successful FUNdation Run 2025
[Image: Gordon College Celebrates 26th Founding Anniversary with Successful FUNdation Run 2025]
[Alumni](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/alumni/) [Campus](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/campus/) [GCFAS](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/gcfas/) [News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Friday, February 28, 2025**
Gordon College launched its 26th Founding Anniversary festivities through FUNdation Run 2025, which took place on February 23rd.
Gordon College Faculty Association (GCFAS), in partnership with Gordon College Alumni Association Inc. (GCAAI), successfully organized the event as many students, faculty members, alumni, and community members attended the celebration.
Among the distinguished guests present were Hon. Sarah Lugerna Lipumano-Garcia, Olongapo City Councilor; Dr. Imelda D.P. Soriano, College President; Ms. Agnes L. Melo, GCFAS President; and Mr. Joseph Angelo B. Pusing, GCAAI President.
They joined GCFAS and GCAAI officers, college officials, administrative staff, faculty, students, alumni, and numerous college supporters in making the event a resounding success.
Jeian Espiritu emerged as the winner in the Boys Student Category, completing the race in an impressive 10 minutes and 44 seconds.
“I was motivated to run by my teammates in the Gordon College athletics program and my girlfriend,” Espiritu shared. “Winning feels great but also adds pressure for future years.”
In the women’s Student Category, Susie May Mistica Ariño took first place with a time of 14 minutes and 43 seconds.
Ariño credited her partner’s encouragement and her focus on mental health for her success. “It started when my partner encouraged me to run,” Ariño explained.
“While running, I realized I wanted more than just a casual run for the sake of my mental health. I started joining his training plans until he gifted me a running watch.”
Furthermore, Nicole Bernal Marcial, an alumna of Gordon College, won the Alumni Category with a time of 14 minutes and 32 seconds.
“The FUNdation Run isn’t just about promoting fitness and health—it’s a way to celebrate and commemorate Gordon College’s 26th founding anniversary,” Marcial said.
“As an alumnus, I wanted to be part of this special occasion.”
He also emphasized the importance of community and the joy of running for his participation.
The winners also offered advice to aspiring runners.
Espiritu encouraged them to persevere even when facing challenges.
Meanwhile, Ariño stressed the importance of preparation and a winner’swinner’s mindset.
Lastly, Marcial advised runners to enjoy the process and find their motivation. “The hardest part of joining fun runs or any running event is finding the motivation to start. But once you understand why you’re doing it and learn to love the experience, everything else follows, ” he said.
He added, “One foot in front of the other, and always be proud of yourself for taking that step.”
The FUNdation Run 2025 served as a fitting start to Gordon College’s 26th Founding Anniversary, as it brought together the college community and promoted health and wellness.

# Clean As You Go & Bring Your Own Trash Policy
[Image: Clean As You Go & Bring Your Own Trash Policy]
**Friday, August 8, 2025**
Instructions for Gordon College Students: Clean As You Go & Bring Your Own Trash Policy
Purpose:
To foster a clean and respectful campus environment while promoting sustainability through personal responsibility for waste.
Before Class or Activity:
1. Prepare Your Materials:
– Bring Your Own Trash: Carry a small, reusable bag or container to collect any waste you generate during class or activities. This could be a sturdy tote, a lunch bag, or any suitable container.
– Plan for Snacks/Drinks: If you plan to consume food or beverages, pack them in a way that minimizes waste (e.g., reusable containers, bottles).
During Class or Activity:
2. Maintain Your Space:
– Keep Your Area Clean: Throughout the session, stay vigilant about your surroundings. Avoid leaving papers, wrappers, or any personal items strewn about.
– Immediate Clean-Up: If you create a mess (accidental spills, paper cuts, etc.), address it promptly. If cleaning supplies are available, use them to tidy up immediately.
3. Responsible Waste Management:
– Use Your Reusable Container: Whenever you have waste, place it in your reusable bag or container. Keep it nearby for easy access.
– Respect Shared Spaces: Be mindful of not just your space but also those around you. Dispose of any common area waste (e.g., napkins from community snacks) in your own trash.
After Class or Activity:
4. Final Cleanup:
– Inspect Your Area:
Before leaving, take a moment to ensure your seating area and any communal spaces (tables, chairs) are tidy.
– Empty Your Trash into Appropriate Bins: When you leave the classroom or activity, empty your reusable container at designated trash or recycling bins outside the classroom (if available). Take anything that belongs to you with you.
5. Dispose Responsibly:
– Recycle When Possible: If your waste is recyclable, place it in the recycling bin. Be sure to check the college’s recycling guidelines to ensure proper disposal.
Additional Responsibilities:
6. Encourage a Culture of Cleanliness:
– Remind Peers:If you notice a classmate leaving a mess, gently remind them or offer to help.
– Lead by Example: Demonstrating your commitment to the “Clean As You Go” policy can inspire your peers to do the same.
7. Feedback and Improvement:
– Participate in discussions or feedback sessions organized by the college to share your insights on how the Clean As You Go policy is working.
8. Engage with Initiatives:
– Stay updated on any college-led environmental initiatives or clean-up days, and participate actively when you can.
By adhering to these instructions, you contribute to creating a cleaner, more sustainable campus environment while developing valuable habits of personal responsibility and community stewardship. Thank you for doing your part!

# DISINFECTION OF GORDON COLLEGE MAIN AND ANNEX BUILDINGS DUE TO RISING CASES OF INFLUENZA
[Image: DISINFECTION OF GORDON COLLEGE MAIN AND ANNEX BUILDINGS DUE TO RISING CASES OF INFLUENZA]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Friday, October 17, 2025**
Due to the rising cases of Influenza-like illnesses, the City Health Office conducts disinfection procedures at 1:00pm, October 17, Gordon College Main and Annex Building.
With this, Face-to-face classes shifted to online mode in the afternoon and will resume the following day, October 18.
Students and campus personnel who are experiencing symptoms of flu are advised to wear a face mask to ensure safety.| Jasmine Zeah Y. Llagas /The FOREFRONT

# LPCC IKOT PALENGKE PROJECT METRO: Monitorning Enforcement and Tracking Resource Outline
[Image: LPCC IKOT PALENGKE PROJECT METRO: Monitorning Enforcement and Tracking Resource Outline]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Thursday, January 15, 2026**
January 15, 2026 | DTI Zambales initial coordination meeting with Gordon College for the development of LPCC Ikot Palengke PROJECT METRO: Monitoring Enforcement & Tracking Resource Online.
The LPCC Ikot Palengke Project METRO: Monitoring Enforcement & Tracking Resource Online is a digital system intended to support government operations in consumer protection, price monitoring, fair trade enforcement, and public service delivery. The project aims to modernize data collection, reporting, monitoring, and analytics through the use of information systems and emerging technologies.

# MX GC PRIDE 2024 Candidates
[Image: MX GC PRIDE 2024 Candidates]
[OSWS](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/osws/)
**Monday, February 5, 2024**
𝐌𝐞𝐞𝐭 𝐭𝐡𝐞 𝐂𝐚𝐧𝐝𝐢𝐝𝐚𝐭𝐞𝐬 𝐨𝐟 𝐌𝐱. 𝐆𝐂 𝐏𝐫𝐢𝐝𝐞 𝟐𝟎𝟐𝟒!
[Image: 🌟]
From the bold to the brilliant, these candidates embody the spirit of diversity and pride.
Get ready to be captivated as we proudly present the fierce faces vying for the coveted crown.
Who will be the first title holder of Mx. GC Pride?
𝗩𝗼𝘁𝗶𝗻𝗴 𝘀𝘁𝗮𝗿𝘁𝘀 𝗻𝗼𝘄! The candidate with the highest number of engagement (heart reacts and share) will win the 𝗠𝘅. 𝗦𝗼𝗰𝗶𝗮𝗹 𝗠𝗲𝗱𝗶𝗮 award during the coronation night on Feb. 20, 2024.

### Source: https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/guideline/avoid-cellphone-use-on-stairs

# Avoid Cellphone Use on Stairs
[Image: Avoid Cellphone Use on Stairs]
**Friday, April 17, 2026**
**Safety Reminder Regarding Cellphone Use on Stairways**  
To ensure the safety of all students and faculty, we are reminding everyone of the following guideline regarding electronic device usage on stairs:
**Policy:**  
Cellphone use is strictly prohibited while ascending or descending staircases. This includes texting, browsing social media, making calls, or playing games.
**Rationale:**  
Stairways are high-traffic areas that require full attention. Using a cellphone while walking significantly reduces spatial awareness and reaction time, increasing the risk of:
* Slips, trips and falls
* Collisions with other students
* Blocking the flow of traffic during passing periods
**Procedure:**
* **Pause:** If you must send a message or answer a call, step to the side and stop walking before using your device.
* **Pocket:** Keep phones stored in pockets or bags while navigating steps.
* **Proceed:** Only resume walking once the device is put away and your full attention is on the stairs.
Thank you for helping us keep our campus safe.

# GC Welcomes Konyang University of South Korea
[Image: GC Welcomes Konyang University of South Korea]
[IPDEA](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/ipdea/) [News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Wednesday, May 14, 2025**
On May 14, 2025, Gordon College warmly welcomed delegates from Konyang University, South Korea, as part of an initiative to explore academic collaboration between the two institutions. The delegation was composed of Ms. Youngmi Sohn, Head of the Global Education Innovation Headquarters, and Mr. Dong-Yeon Ko, Team Leader.
The visit aimed to strengthen international ties, particularly in the field of Allied Health Studies, and included a tour of the college’s facilities—classrooms, laboratories, and library—especially in relation to Konyang’s interest in developing a short-term language program.
During the meeting, the delegates expressed their interest in discussing various opportunities for collaboration and confirmed that they are currently reviewing the proposed Memorandum of Agreement (MOA). Both institutions expressed optimism for a sustainable and meaningful partnership that supports global academic engagement and student development.

Tulong Dunong Program (TDP) and Tertiary Education Subsidy (TES) Distribution

[Image: 📅]
Date: February 24, 2026 (Tuesday)
[Image: ⏰]
Time: 9:00 AM – 4:00 PM
[Image: 📍]
Venue: Room 415, Gordon College – Main Campus
This payout covers the following:
• TDP Batch 3 – 2nd Semester, Academic Year 2024–2025
• TES Listahanan 15 – 2nd Semester, Academic Year 2024–2025
[Image: 📄]
Required Documents
Please bring the following complete requirements:
1. Three (3) photocopies of your student ID or valid government ID (with signature), each with three (3) specimen signatures.

[Image: 🔔]

# GC produces 9 new CPAs; yields 39.13% pass rate in October CPALE
[Image: GC produces 9 new CPAs; yields 39.13% pass rate in October CPALE]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Tuesday, November 4, 2025**
Nine alumni from the College of Business and Accountancy (CBA) of Gordon College (GC) were among the passers of the October Certified Public Accountant Licensure Exam (CPALE) per Professional Regulatory Board of Accountancy, on November 4.
GC garnered an overall passing rate of 39.13% from 9 passers out of 23 takers, surpassing the national passing rate of 34.02%. These constitute the 3,460 newly registered Certified Public Accountants (CPA).
Comprising this are three first-time takers and six repeater examinees.
In addition, Mike Ronnel Castro of Pampanga State University (for. Don Honorario Ventura State University) topped the examination with a 91.83% rating.
Bicol University – Daraga is the lone institution in the list of top-performing schools with 50 or more examinees with an 84.85% passing rate.
The licensure exam was conducted from October 24 to 26. | via Keane Rafael Abdon/The FOREFRONT

# LCUAA 2025 Welcomes Rainy Sunday Afternoon
[Image: LCUAA 2025 Welcomes Rainy Sunday Afternoon]
[LCUAA](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/lcuaa/) [News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Sunday, October 19, 2025**
The eagerly anticipated week-long 14th LCUAA National Games officially kicked off today at the City of San Jose del Monte (CSJDM) Sports Complex.
Cheers and applause filled the venue as the opening ceremony began with a parade featuring all 27 participating colleges, each led by their institution’s gold medalists.
Following the parade was the introduction of the LCUAA 2025 representative officers, a doxology by the Sining Tanglawan ng San Jose del Monte Performing Group, the singing of the National Anthem and the San Jose del Monte city hymn, and an energetic dance performance by the San Joseño World Class Talents troupe.
City College of San Jose del Monte (CCSJDM) College President Dr. Roger S. Ambida delivered the opening remarks, warmly welcoming delegates to the institution.
Hon. Arturo B. Robes then gave the keynote address, encouraging athletes to build a brighter and more empowered future.
Additionally, Dr. Lora L. Yusi, CHED Region 3 Director IV, gave an inspiring speech, highlighting the significance of LCUAA 2025 as a testament to the growth of local universities: “We see scholars who dream larger than themselves.”
The competitive events officially begin tomorrow, October 20, 2025.
Stay tuned to the official Facebook page of The Forefront for updates on the 14th LCUAA National Games. | via Alyssa Marie Alcantara / The FOREFRONT

# MRPs Tree Planting
[Image: MRPs Tree Planting]
[Extension](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/extension/) [RDCES](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/rdces/) [Community Extension](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/community-extension/)

The event was successfully conducted with active participation from students, faculty members, and administrative personnel from the GC community. Our strong commitment to environmental sustainability and community engagement drove our involvement in this initiative. We firmly believe that by fostering the active engagement of our employees and volunteers in such endeavors, we exemplify our organizational values and reinforce our dedication to corporate social responsibility.

# Empowering GFPS members through the Application of Harmonized Gender and Development Guidelines
[Image: Empowering GFPS members through the Application of Harmonized Gender and Development Guidelines]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Tuesday, June 17, 2025**
The Gordon College, through its Diversity, Equity, and Inclusion Unit as the GC-GFPS Secretariat, successfully facilitated a seminar for members of the Gordon College Gender and Development Focal Point System (GC-GFPS) entitled “Empowering GFPS Members through the Application of the Harmonized Gender and Development Guidelines” on June 13, 2025, held at the GC Library Audio-Visual Room.
This capacity-building initiative was organized to further strengthen the College’s gender mainstreaming efforts. It aimed to equip GC-GFPS members with the essential knowledge and practical skills needed to effectively integrate gender perspectives into the institution’s programs, projects, and activities. The seminar primarily focused on the application of the Harmonized Gender and Development Guidelines (HGDG)—a critical framework designed to ensure that development initiatives are gender-responsive and aligned with the overarching goals of gender equality and women’s empowerment.
[#sdg5genderequality](https://www.facebook.com/hashtag/sdg5genderequality?__eep__=6&__cft__[0]=AZUdoZMQt1jGKjoX0IeOuh51XYw-kIbu31Nf4ujIxdo5aNYr1MW6_oVy_1u7WZ0_v6IP3dDTRqgYrxFR5XkaR8mT5NxM0pE1wIF5tFIflV4nolIlYJRxgx-K98aTKThwBWkXYnC9RG-JDbx-52QvXJ5sjuKaILdsb1Iiltahaz1W-7W-6D7hdukVkhPj7XiojwwomO4TPWlVqe86lejzzQjK2K7vU6DLkTqizfbMjr5ZvA&__tn__=*NK-y-R)
[#SDG17partnershipsforthegoals](https://www.facebook.com/hashtag/sdg17partnershipsforthegoals?__eep__=6&__cft__[0]=AZUdoZMQt1jGKjoX0IeOuh51XYw-kIbu31Nf4ujIxdo5aNYr1MW6_oVy_1u7WZ0_v6IP3dDTRqgYrxFR5XkaR8mT5NxM0pE1wIF5tFIflV4nolIlYJRxgx-K98aTKThwBWkXYnC9RG-JDbx-52QvXJ5sjuKaILdsb1Iiltahaz1W-7W-6D7hdukVkhPj7XiojwwomO4TPWlVqe86lejzzQjK2K7vU6DLkTqizfbMjr5ZvA&__tn__=*NK-y-R)

### Source: https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/%f0%9d%90%8f%f0%9d%90%9a%f0%9d%90%a0%f0%9d%90%a5%f0%9d%90%a2%f0%9d%90%a5%f0%9d%90%a2%f0%9d%90%a9%f0%9d%90%9a%f0%9d%90%ad-%f0%9d%90%a7%f0%9d%90%a0-%f0%9d%90%a4%f0%9d%90%9a%f0%9d%90%a9%f0%9d%90%9a

# 𝐏𝐚𝐠𝐥𝐢𝐥𝐢𝐩𝐚𝐭 𝐧𝐠 𝐤𝐚𝐩𝐚𝐧𝐠𝐲𝐚𝐫𝐢𝐡𝐚𝐧 𝐬𝐚 𝐛𝐚𝐠𝐨𝐧𝐠 𝐭𝐞𝐫𝐦𝐢𝐧𝐨, 𝐩𝐨𝐫𝐦𝐚𝐥 𝐧𝐚𝐧𝐠 𝐧𝐚𝐢𝐬𝐚𝐤𝐚𝐭𝐮𝐩𝐚𝐫𝐚𝐧
[Image: 𝐏𝐚𝐠𝐥𝐢𝐥𝐢𝐩𝐚𝐭 𝐧𝐠 𝐤𝐚𝐩𝐚𝐧𝐠𝐲𝐚𝐫𝐢𝐡𝐚𝐧 𝐬𝐚 𝐛𝐚𝐠𝐨𝐧𝐠 𝐭𝐞𝐫𝐦𝐢𝐧𝐨, 𝐩𝐨𝐫𝐦𝐚𝐥 𝐧𝐚𝐧𝐠 𝐧𝐚𝐢𝐬𝐚𝐤𝐚𝐭𝐮𝐩𝐚𝐫𝐚𝐧]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Friday, July 18, 2025**
GORDON COLLEGE — Isinalin na ang mga posisyon at kapangyarihan sa mga bagong opisyales, gayundin ang pagpapakilala sa mga bagong kakatawan sa mga GCians sa katatapos na Supreme Student Council Turnover Ceremony na ginanap sa PE Hall nitong ika-14 ng Hulyo.
Nasaksihan din ng mga lider-estudyante mula sa iba’t ibang organisasyon sa loob ng institusyon ang nabanggit na seremonya.
Bilang panimula, binigyang diin ng noo’y SSC Chairperson Frances Daphne Mobo ang seremonya sa paglalahad ng Budget at Accomplishment Reports ng kanyang termino.
Samantala, inamin ni Mobo na nabigo nilang tuparin ang ilang mga pangakong proyekto para sa mga mag-aaral.
“Failures make us better individuals. Leadership teaches you how to be accountable [for] your own actions and how to accept constructive criticism. To our student leaders present here today, do remember that leadership is not about positions or titles because those are temporary. Leadership is about passion and dedication,” aniya.
Bukod dito, binigyan ng pagkakataon ang bagong termino upang talakayin at bigyang linaw ang kanilang mga inihandang proyekto at aktibidades sa harap ng kanilang mga kapwa lider-estudyante.
Sumatutal, mayroong 12 na proyekto at 17 na aktibidades na gustong ilunsad ang naturang termino sa pangunguna ni ngayo’y SSC Chairperson Julier Samonte. Ilan dito ay ang GCLAMP 2.0: Enhancing Access in the GCLAMP, CODE 200: Tech Industry Partnership Found, BIN-novation: Classroom for a Cleaner Future para sa kanilang proyekto, samantala ay inahain naman ang Student First Starter Packs: College Life Unboxed, Think Green: Green Revolutions for GCians, Beyond the Myths: Understanding HIV/AIDS & Prevention para sa kanilang mga aktibidades.
Ngunit ang lahat ng kanilang programa ay pawang mga panukala pa lamang at posibleng mayroong ibang hindi mapayagang mailunsad, paglilinaw ng bagong konseho.
Bilang karagdagan sa mga pangako ni Samonte, bagong kinatawan ng konseho, nais niya at ng kaniyang konseho na palawakin ang komunikasyon at transparency sa pagsasagawa ng regular student consultations, open forums, at online suggestion platforms para marinig ang tunay na saloobin ng mga estudyante. Kasama rin dito ang paglabas ng general plan of actions, budget breakdowns, at accomplishment reports upang mas mapanatili ang tiwala ng bawat estudyante sa konseho.
“Pangatlo, mas makabuluhang events para sa lahat. Gagawin nating inclusive at meaningful ang bawat SSC-led event. Hindi lang ito basta kasiyahan dahil gagawa rin po tayo ng mga aktibidad na magtataguyod ng leadership, advocacy, at student development.”
“Pang apat, pagpapalakas ng bawat student organization sa bawat departamento. Bilang inyong chairperson, sisiguraduhin kong makakaramdam ng buong suporta ang bawat departamental organization,” dagdag pa niya.
Paalala naman ng bagong SSC Chairperson na ang kaniyang pagkapanalo noong nakaraang eleksyon ay hindi lamang tagumpay ng isang tao kundi tagumpay rin ng bawat estudyante na naniniwala na pwedeng marinig, makilahok, at maging bahagi ng pagbabago.

# GC honors DASArving alumni, highlights iconic “first-times” in 4th DASA
[Image: GC honors DASArving alumni, highlights iconic “first-times” in 4th DASA]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Tuesday, October 14, 2025**
SMX OLONGAPO CENTRAL— The 4th Distinguished Alumni Service Awards (DASA) 2025 gathered alumni who paved innovation and inspiration for Gordon College on October 11, held at SMX Olongapo Central.
Mr. Joseph Pusing, former Gordon College Alumni Association Inc. (GCAAI) President, proudly presented all the first-time projects that happened on the initiative of giving back to their alma mater: Alumni cards, Financial support for the student council and organizations, Cosme Y. Sering Library, and a fifty thousand cash donation for the College of Business and Accountancy (CBA) Department for the extension of rooms for accreditation.
“One of the highlights of our term is the donation of the alumni association’s newest student lounge, which was blessed on August 15, 2025. This will not be possible without the help and guidance of everyone,” he stated.
Also, Dr. Imelda DP. Soriano, the college president, exclaimed in her keynote speech that the world needs someone like them who wagers unselfish services in a world full of selfishness.
Furthermore, Ms. Rose Anne Cañeda Dumalo, alumna from the Bachelor of Science in Education – English (BSEd-English) Batch 2015, expressed in her speech that titles and recognition will not define us but the people that we serve along the way.
“Higit sa pagiging magaling ay ang pagiging mabuti. You may be the best in the field, but if you lack character, people will remember how you treated them more than how well you did your job,” she added.
Moreover, Ms. Ellinor T. Manaois-Yco, Bachelor of Science in Nursing (BSN) Batch 2011; Mr. Arben R. Cauilan, Bachelor of Science in Customs Administration (BSCA) Batch 2011; Nikki Antonette Chieng Carlos, Bachelor of Science in Tourism (BSTM); and Mr. Willy R. Antigo, Master of Arts in Education (MAEd) Batch 2019, were awarded with recognitions and plaques for their outstanding service and contributions.
In addition, Ms. Lovelyn P. Ceralde, DASA 2025 Overall Chairperson, extended her warm welcome and gratitude to the alumni, stakeholders, and those who have been bringing their best to provide a more quality education and experience inside the institution.
Finally, the program ended with an oath-taking for the newly elected GCAAI officers and board of trustees for the fiscal year 2025 – 2026. | via John Patrick Mateo/The FOREFRONT

# GC Welcomes 5 new Registered Midwifes, Perfect passing in November MLE
[Image: GC Welcomes 5 new Registered Midwifes, Perfect passing in November MLE]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Wednesday, November 19, 2025**
Five alumni from the College of Allied Health and Services (CAHS) of Gordon College (GC) passed the Midwives Licensure Exam (MLE) according to the Professional Regulation Commission Board.
GC achieved a perfect passing rate of 100% with 5 passers out of 5 examinees, once again surpassing the rate of last year’s results of 93.48% and the national rate of 57.60%. They constitute the 2,152 newly registered midwives.
All are first-time takers of this year’s exam.
Additionally, Tagaloan Community College is the top-performing school in the licensure exam with a perfect passing rate from 85 examinees of the school.
Meanwhile, Princesa Dumale Talamayan, this year’s board topnotcher, from Palawan State University achieved a 94.00%.
The licensure exam was held on November 8-9 and 16. | via Roi Chester B. Manio/The FOREFRONT

# Ang Paghatak ni Apolo ng Karwahe sa Dulo ng PaSIKLABan 2025
[Image: Ang Paghatak ni Apolo ng Karwahe sa Dulo ng PaSIKLABan 2025]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Tuesday, September 30, 2025**
OLONGAPO CITY—Ang pagtaklob ng ulap sa nakapapasong araw ay naging tanda ng pagtatapos ng SIKLAB 2025. Sa pagkalansing ng medalya at pagkinang ng tropeyo, umalingawngaw ang sigawan at palakpakan. Kagat-labi ang mga manonood sa antisipasyon kung sino ang magkakamit ng inaasam na pagkapanalo.
Bago parangalan ang magkakampeon sa sagupaan ng mga pating, tigre, wizards, phoenix, at mentor, nagbigay ng natatanging mensahe si Dr. Imelda DP. Soriano na tunay na nagbigay konklusyon sa limang araw na bakbakan sa palarong pampalakasan.
Sa huli, isa lang ang tanong na namutawi: mananatili bang asul ang kulay ng kampeon o mamamayagpag ang bandila ng ibang kolehiyo? | via Kana Maye Dueñas/The FOREFRONT

# Blessing of Gordon College Annex Building
[Image: Blessing of Gordon College Annex Building]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Monday, August 11, 2025**
Pormal na binasbasan ang bagong Annex Building ng Gordon College ngayong Agosto 11, 2025, sa pangunguna ni Rev. Fr. Roque Villanueva.
Dumalo sa makabuluhang seremonya sina Mayor Atty. Rolen C. Paulino Jr., BCDA Director Rolen C. Paulino, Gordon College President Dr. Imelda D.P. Soriano, mga Konsehal ng Lungsod, at ilan pang opisyal, kasama ang mga estudyante, guro, at kawani ng Gordon College bilang pagsuporta sa makasaysayang pagbubukas ng bagong gusali.
Mahigit sa tatlong libong karagdagang estudyante ang makikinabang sa bagong gusali.
Itinakda ang pagbubukas ng Annex Building kasabay ng pasimula ng klase ngayong Academic Year 2025–2026, bilang bahagi ng patuloy na pagtugon ng lokal na pamahalaan at pamunuan ng kolehiyo sa lumalaking pangangailangan para sa dekalidad at makabagong pasilidad sa edukasyon.
Courtesy to [**Olongapo City Information Center**](https://www.facebook.com/olongapopublicaffairs?__cft__[0]=AZUoEEuU7JRBp8m9YZ_lMtmfx9IJRxP901v3h3T0hfeZn1kxjLV0Z1r6Jfs3Bag4ifapazsLBegn1V1TQu1yB6pyZZx5ZTFUaZUlZqA2TOCdxP8_aqb4eGNYK49-vrS4sSl1XTuYTylL_EcYgARMMYYnCv7KUeZIwb2Y985F8OVk2jWSh389TouCTzffLa23nDTYIT4g6th1iQvxaJMV5SncNFYJ5OXzmrj-OwOukqkGvw&__tn__=-UC%2CP-y-R). Read full article [here](https://www.facebook.com/olongapopublicaffairs/posts/pfbid02Bss2CRG99Jb9rXr2nYMB6CQ7p5cWsYinmTc1Lh32eBMQ1V73JH1xNo6fxvSiRV7gl?__cft__[0]=AZUoEEuU7JRBp8m9YZ_lMtmfx9IJRxP901v3h3T0hfeZn1kxjLV0Z1r6Jfs3Bag4ifapazsLBegn1V1TQu1yB6pyZZx5ZTFUaZUlZqA2TOCdxP8_aqb4eGNYK49-vrS4sSl1XTuYTylL_EcYgARMMYYnCv7KUeZIwb2Y985F8OVk2jWSh389TouCTzffLa23nDTYIT4g6th1iQvxaJMV5SncNFYJ5OXzmrj-OwOukqkGvw&__tn__=%2CO%2CP-y-R).

# CHTM Sharks Roar at 2nd CHTM Rally 2025
[Image: CHTM Sharks Roar at 2nd CHTM Rally 2025]
[CHTM](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/chtm/) [News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Thursday, September 11, 2025**
GORDON COLLEGE — The College of Hospitality and Tourism Management (CHTM) filled the East Tapinac Covered Court with cheers and chants as the 2nd CHTM Rally unfolded last September 9, 2025, igniting the spirit of the CHTM Sharks in preparation for the much-anticipated Siklab 2025 Sportsfest on September 15–19, 2025.
The event showcased the final lineup of the College of Hospitality and Tourism Management (CHTM) official teams and players.
Furthermore, athletes from the CHTM Sharks introduced themselves through lively intermission numbers performed by each sports team, adding excitement and entertainment to the rally.
Player representatives from each team also participated in a brief interview with the Masters of Ceremony, where they shared their thoughts and enthusiasm for the upcoming Siklab competition.
Moreover, the event was organized in collaboration with the College of Hospitality and Tourism Management Student Council (CHTM-SC), Arapaap Productions, the Junior Association of Hospitality Management Students (JAHMS), and the League of Tourism Students of the Philippines (LTSP), who worked together to ensure the program’s success.
The College of Hospitality and Tourism Management (CHTM) Dean, Dr. Mark Alvin Lazaro, Assistant Dean Vincent Dela Cruz, Bachelor of Science and Tourism Management (BSTM) Program Coordinator Ma’am Lizette Ann P. Sia, Bachelor of Science in Hospitality Management (BSHM) Coordinator Vince Richard Gomez, and ARAPAAP Adviser Ms. Jenny Mae M. Lagman also extended strong support and leadership, which greatly guided the preparations for the rally.
To cap off the event, the atmosphere reached its peak as the CHTM Sharks filled the covered court with their department’s official Siklab cheer, embodying their spirit of unity and readiness for the upcoming sportsfest.| via Lovely Doroin/The FOREFRONT

# World University Rankings 2026: GC Recognized as Reporter Institution
[Image: World University Rankings 2026: GC Recognized as Reporter Institution]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Saturday, October 18, 2025**
Gordon College has officially been granted Reporter Status in the recent Times Higher Education (THE) World University Rankings 2026, released last October 9.
The college is among six Higher Education Institutions (HEIs) in Central Luzon that have been granted this recognition, including:  
– Bulacan State University  
– Central Luzon State University  
– Nueva Ecija University of Science and Technology  
– Tarlac Agricultural University, and  
– City College of San Fernando Pampanga
The Times Higher Education annually releases their World University Rankings that measure the performance of universities in eighteen (18) performance indicators across five core pillars: teaching, research environment, research quality, international outlook, and industry. A reporter status is granted to HEIs who have submitted relevant data but did not meet eligibility criteria to receive a rank. Inclusion in the reporter status allows HEIs to receive feedback in their performance across the metrics to support future decision making.
Meanwhile, Ateneo de Manila University is the highest ranking university in the Philippines with a banded rank of 1001-1200, followed by the University of the Philippines (1201-1500), De la Salle University (1501+), Mapua University (1501+). Mindanao State University – Iligan Institute of Technology (1501+), and University of Santo Tomas (1501+). The University of Oxford remains to be the top global ranking university for the tenth consecutive year. | via Lance Isaac Leon/The FOREFRONT
Sources: Times Higher Education World University Rankings 2026 and CHED Regional Office III (via Facebook)

# CCS Phoenix Clinches Gold at SIKLAB 2025 E-Games
[Image: CCS Phoenix Clinches Gold at SIKLAB 2025 E-Games]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Wednesday, September 17, 2025**
FUNCTION HALL, GORDON COLLEGE MAIN BLDG.—The Gordon College Main Building Function Hall buzzed with excitement as SIKLAB 2025 E-Games came to a spectacular close, featuring intense battles for gold, silver, and bronze.
In the Battle for Bronze, the College of Education, Arts, and Science (CEAS) Mentors defeated the College of Allied Health Studies (CAHS) Tigers, 22-8, securing third place and bringing pride to the CEAS community.
Meanwhile, the championship series between the CCS Phoenix and the CHTM Sharks was a nail-biter in a best-of-three format. CCS edged CHTM in Game 1, 21-20, followed by a 17-win in Game 2. In the final showdown, the Phoenix dominated, 12-1, clinching the gold medal with an overall 2-1 victory.
The CHTM Sharks earned the silver medal, demonstrating remarkable perseverance and strategy throughout the finals.
SIKLAB 2025 E-Games concluded as a remarkable showcase of determination, strategy, and camaraderie, crowning the CCS Phoenix as champions while bringing the excitement of competitive E-sports to Gordon College—and leaving fans eagerly anticipating next year’s edition. | via Frances Marie Farne/The FOREFRONT

# Bagong Lakan at Lakambini ng Kasaysayan, pinasinayaan sa Gordon College
[Image: Bagong Lakan at Lakambini ng Kasaysayan, pinasinayaan sa Gordon College]
[CEAS](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/tag/ceas/) [News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Sunday, September 7, 2025**
GORDON COLLEGE—Inukit na ang mga bagong lakan at lakambini ng kasaysayan kasabay ng panapos na selebrasyon ng Buwan ng Kasaysayan 2025 na may temang “Diwa ng Kasaysayan, Kabilin sa Kabataan” na idinaos noong Agosto 30, sa Gordon College Physical Education (PE) Hall sa pangunguna ng Samahan ng mga Mag-aaral sa Araling Panlipunan (SMAP).
Nagwagi sina G. Lorenzen Rob Gonzales mula sa BSEd Soc 3-A at Bb. Angel Mae Deseo mula sa BSEd Soc 1-A para sa Lakan at Lakambini ng Kasaysayan 2025.
Nasungkit naman nina G. Jhan Girbaud Hipolito mula sa BSEd Soc 2-A at Bb. Jhade Aizelle Quiocho mula sa BSEd Soc 1-A ang korona bilang Ginoong Unang Gantimpala at Binibining Unang Gantimpala.
Namayagpag din bilang Ginoong Ikalawang Gantimpala at Binibining Ikalawang Gantimpala sina G. Rafael Ellado mula sa BSEd Soc 1-A at Bb. Gervy Sarmiento mula sa BSEd Soc 2-A.
Bukod sa Lakan at Lakambini 2025, iginawad din ang mga espesyal na parangal tulad ng Lunting Diwa at Best in Talent na parehong nakuha nina G. Jhan Girbaud Hipolito at Bb. Jhade Aizelle Quiocho.
Nakamit naman nina G. Lorenzen Rob Gonzales at Bb. Jhade Aizelle Quiocho ang mga titulong Best in Formal Attire at People’s Choice Award.
Samantala, inuwi naman nina Bb. Angel Mae Deseo at G. Lorenzen Rob Gonzales ang karangalang Binibini at Ginoo ng Nakaraan.
“Nung sinabi na ako yung panalo, naging proud ako kasi nagbunga yung suporta ng pamilya at mga kaibigan, higit sa lahat, nagbunga yung effort at tiwala ko sa sarili” saad ng Lakan 2025.
“In-expect ko talaga na may chance akong manalo.” Ibinahagi din ni Lorenzen na pinaghirapan niya ang kanyang preparasyon, mula ensayo hanggang pagpapakilala at pagsagot sa tanong ng mga hurado.
Samantala, labis naman ang pasasalamat ni Bb. Angel Mae Deseo, Lakambini 2025, sa lahat ng tumulong sa kanya lalo na at noong panahong iyon ay masama pa ang kanyang karamdaman.
“Tinrangkaso po ako hanggang sa mismong laban, sa kabila nun ay ipinagpatuloy ko ang laban sapagkat nakikita ko ang aking mga kamag-aral (SOC 1-A) na nagtutulong-tulong upang matapos ang lahat ng aming kakailanganin,” saad ni Angel Mae Deseo.
“Lahat ng pagod at puyat ay naging makabuluhan sapagkat nasungkit namin ang korona at karangalan,” aniya. | via Lovely Doroin/The FOREFRONT

# Rights and Obligations of GCAAI Members
#### Rights of Members
All members, regular and honorary, who complied with all the requirements, guidelines, and policies set forth by the Association are members in good standing.
Every member in good standing shall have the following rights:
1. To attend the regular and special meetings of the general membership of the Association;
2. To vote and be elected into office;
3. To propose amendments and resolutions, and to vote on those presented at the meetings above mentioned;
4. To request access to official records, documents, and papers pertaining to the acts, transactions, or decisions of the Association unless otherwise specified;
5. To use the properties and facilities of the Association according to the rules and regulations agreed upon for this purpose;
6. Such other rights and privileges as may be granted by the Board of Trustees.
#### Article 4 Section 5 – The right to vote and be elected as Trustees
The right to vote and be elected as Trustees of this Association shall be exclusively granted to Active Members and members in good standing. Provided, they are listed in the SEC Membership Book/and other forms of registration conducted by the Association and shall be certified correct by the Corporate Secretary. Provided, further, that only active members shall be appointed to any position in the Association.
#### Article 4 Section 6
It is understood that those who have been accepted members of the Association prior to the effectivity of the present By-Laws shall continue to be active members. Provided, further, that after the first general assembly and election, they shall satisfy the requirements stipulated under Section 3.
#### Duties and Obligations of Members
1. Every member, whether regular or honorary, has the responsibility to abide in this Constitution and Bylaws, and rules and regulations set forth by the GC-AA.
2. Every member must pay membership fees and annual fees in an amount determined by the majority vote of the GC-AA Executive Committee and Board. All dues payments shall be made to the treasurer and/or duly representative of the Association.
3. Every member must support and promote the thrusts and objectives of the GC-AA and the College.
4. Every member must participate actively in all Gordon College activities and GC-AA programs and projects.
5. Every member must exercise his/her rights and do his/her responsibilities as a GC-AA member.
6. Every member shall be entitled to exercise full membership rights, including the right to vote and hold office within the Association in accordance with the By-laws.
#### Disciplinary Action Against Members
The GC-AA Board of Trustees shall review and act upon all disputes regarding infractions of Association rules and regulations. The Trustees can form an Ad Hoc Committee that can render decisions in terminating a member from the Association.
The final decision of the said committee shall become final upon the approval of the GC-AA Board of Trustees at its regular monthly or special meeting. The GC-AA Board may overrule the Committee by a two-thirds (2/3) vote.

# Artistry and Unity Take Center Stage at PASE Community Concert 2026
[Image: Artistry and Unity Take Center Stage at PASE Community Concert 2026]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Wednesday, February 25, 2026**
The PASE Community Concert 2026, held on the 2nd day of the 27th Founding Anniversary celebration and in observance of National Arts Month, became a memorable showcase of talent and creativity. The program featured performances from Pase Ballo, Pase Voci, Pase Teatro, and Pase Cuerdas.
The concert opened with dance performances from PASE Ballo, followed by a singing presentation from PASE Voci, and an acting performance from PASE Teatro, with each group having its own spotlight to showcase their artistry and skills. It marked the first time that all PASE groups performed together on one stage while highlighting their unique talents individually.
The presentation celebrated unity, creativity, and the passion for the arts, making the community concert a meaningful part of the anniversary and National Arts Month celebration.

# 𝘼 𝙇𝙚𝙜𝙖𝙘𝙮 𝙤𝙛 𝙀𝙭𝙘𝙚𝙡𝙡𝙚𝙣𝙘𝙚, 𝘼 𝙁𝙪𝙩𝙪𝙧𝙚 𝙤𝙛 𝙄𝙢𝙥𝙖𝙘𝙩
[Image: 𝘼 𝙇𝙚𝙜𝙖𝙘𝙮 𝙤𝙛 𝙀𝙭𝙘𝙚𝙡𝙡𝙚𝙣𝙘𝙚, 𝘼 𝙁𝙪𝙩𝙪𝙧𝙚 𝙤𝙛 𝙄𝙢𝙥𝙖𝙘𝙩]
[News](https://gordoncollege.edu.ph/w3/category/news/)
**Sunday, August 17, 2025**
Gordon College is proud to announce that the Philippine Society of Customs Administration Students (PSCAS) Gordon College Chapter soared to new heights at the PSCAS National Awards on August 16, 2025, at Wind Residences, Tagaytay City!
PSCAS GC Chapter was honored with the most prestigious award: Top Performing PSCAS Chapter!
This incredible achievement is a testament to our dedication to excellence and unwavering commitment to our community.
We also brought home a constellation of awards, including Most Outstanding in:
\* Community Impact & Civic Engagement
\* Leadership & Institutional Development Projects
\* Specialized Customs Training & Webinar Programs
And we were recognized as Outstanding in:
\* Academic Excellence & Professional Development
\* Career Preparation & Skills Development
\* Culture, Arts & Wellness Promotion
\* Environmental Advocacy & Sustainability
\* Student Engagement & Community Building Initiatives
\* Student Support & Mentorship Initiatives
We want to give a special shout-out to two of our very own who stood out among the best students in the country:
\* Kris Rean Agaton was named the Top 1 Most Outstanding BSCA Student of the Philippines 2025.
\* Renmmelle Kyle Cerilles was named among the top 3 most outstanding BSCA Students in the Philippines in 2025.
Your hard work, leadership, and passion have made a mark, and we couldn’t be prouder of your achievements.
This incredible success belongs to every member, officer, and adviser who contributed their time and talent to make our chapter shine.
Thank you for your tireless efforts!
